In no case is there a similar transposition only of responsiones. rev. II: i o Verba mea, que tu in (Y [in ras. fl r2 y F K q [in marg. q] Gh cum P B Ab tamen 0 tu ri) spirituali visione frequenter a me audis, ... With regard to the distribution among the MSS., the reading of the archetype was either tu in or cum. The latter alternative, however, seems more plausible, since the r1 reading tu may be taken to support an assumed cum in the archetype, as weil as tamen in 0 is probably derived from cum; as to the confusion of cum- tu and cum-tamen, cf. above, p. 78 with footnote 9. From the paleographical point of view, either of the readings tu in and cum could have been derived from the other. If cum is correct, then it is reasonable to take cum spirituali visione to mean something like "with a thereto attached vision", i. e. it would imply a certain stress laid upon the fact that Birgitta not only hears but also sees. However, such a stress appears a little unwarranted in the context, and it is avoided in the reading tu in. The latter reading is also supported by in spirituali visone in the heading (line 3); these words may very weil refer to the similar expression in our case. The phrase `hear in a vision' is of course not problematic; according to Alphonso it is even possible to 'hear a vision', Ep. Sol. 4 A gracia videndi et audiendi visiones spiri- tuales. Nor does the presence of tu involve any difficulty. This pronoun (as is the case of other personal pronouns) is, in the Revelations, either taken along or it is omitted, generally without any visible functional difference, cf. int. i o: 4 Item, cum omnia gossis ..., cur ... and int. 16: 2 Item, cum tu sis Deifilius ..., cur ... rev. 12: 8 Hic ignis incendit lampadem cordis eius ad laborandum in honore meo. Et accendit eciam animam ad recipiendum aruinam gracie et verborum meorum, a quibus anima dulciter recipitur (p n Gh reficitur K) et plenius impinguatur, quando ad opera peruenitur. In rev. 12 a man is compared to a lamp; cf. above, p. 36 f. The word ignis in the quotation symbolizes the Holy Spirit, which makes the lamp burn. The man's soul will receive (recipiendum) the Lord's grace and words, symbolized by the oil (aruinam, lit. `tallow'; cf. Rev. 1 52: 13 Verba enim mea sunt quasi aruina,18 IV 98 B huic ego immittam oleum gracie mee); by these his soul dukiter recipitur, and the question is whether this recipitur is really authentic. If recipitur is translated 'is received', the sense must be considered utterly strange: the soul receives grace and words by which it is received. Lunden 2, 305 translates Et accendit ... recipitur by 18 Mr. C.-G. Undhagen kindly called my attention to this passage. 
 
 
 
 
 85 "Den upptänder även själen till att mottaga nådens och mina ords feta olja, av vilka själen, när hon mottager dem, för s ö tas", but it is obvious that this desperate translation is not justified by the Latin. On the other hand, it seems rather probable that Lunden's translation comes closer to the intended meaning of this sentence than does recipitur as translated by 'is received', and we have thus reason to think that the K reading reficitur fits better in with the context, "the soul is invigorated". The resemblance between recipitur and reficitur makes it necessary to consider seriously the possibility that recipitur is an archetypal error for reficitur; ci in the preceding dulciter could also have had some influence. The expression anima reficitur is not problematic, cf. e.g. Rev. 1 33: 5 in mundi sapiencia ... est ... nulla anime refeccio. An early passage, expressing an idea rather similar to the one assumed for verborum ..., a quibus anima dulciter reficitur, is given by Ven. Fort., Carm. 3, 14, 17 Pectora cunctorum reficis dulcedine verbi,18 though the subject of reficis is not at all God but a certain bishop whom the poet addresses. Nor is the adverb dulciter, which is to be compared with dulcedinel9 in the passage from Ven. Fort., problematic in the context. A parallel is furnished by a poem by Petrus Damianus, no. D 8, 5 in M. Lokrantz' edition," miras species saluator confecit, Quibus omnes dulciter electos r efecit. This adverb appears in the Revelations in considerably more remarkable combinations, e.g. I z: 6 Debet eciam sponsa quam dulciter te r eduxi (Lunden 1, 76 "hur ljuvligt jag återlöste attendere dig") and, even more striking, I 58:R Verba Matris ad sponsam et Matris et Klä dulciter adinuicem ("The Mother's words to the bride, and the sweet conversa- tion between the Mother and the Son"; Lunden 1, 177 translates incorrectly "Moderns ord till bruden, och hur ljuvliga modern och Sonen är för varandra"). There are, however, some facts which work against the assumption that recipitur in our case is erroneous. First, the verb reficere seems to be constructed with perso- nal subject in the Revelations (e.g. I 33: 7, III 18 B, IV 47 B, 126 V, Decl. VI 351K, Add. VII 11: 13), which may be regarded as an argument against gracie et reficitur: such a construction would probably presuppose verborum ..., a quibus gracia et verba reficiunt, i.e. an impersonal subject. Nor did an active construction I find in the Revelations examples of reficere in the passive voice combined with a (ab) and the ablative, whereas there are cases with ex (SA 3: 15) and the ablative only (Rev. VII 3: 5); the verb also occurs in the passive voice without any ablative at all in the meaning 'be fed' = `eat' (Ex. 33: 9, 35: 6; cf. Hollman's glossary). This may not be a particularly strong argument; it is of considerably greater interest that Du Cange (s.v. i receptum, vol. 7, p. 43) explicitly says that recipere can have the meaning "receptum dare, seu pastum", and obviously the latter part of that interpretation comes close to reficere, which in our case would make sense in the context according to the reasoning above. To support this sense of the verb recipere 19 Cf. also a letter from Guido de Basochis (circ. 'zoo), in H. Adolfsson's edition (Studia Latina Stockholmiensia 18), p. 79, 7 ff. Vbera uero suggentes, quia r ef eccionis interne dulcedinem trahunt ab euuangelicis apostolicisque doctrinis. 20 Studia Latina Stockholmiensia 12, p. 155. 
 
 
 
 
 86 Du Cange quotes only one example, Et propter hoc debet recipere monachos in refectorio de pane et vino et fabis et piscibus et pimento in festiuitate omnium sanctorum. Unfortunately it was not possible to find the text from which this passage was taken ("Tabularium prioratus de Domina in Delphinatu"), but it appears quite plausible that recipere ... de means something like `feed ... with', the basic meaning `receive ... with' being weakened.21 Du Cange's interpretation of recipere in this passage was accepted by D. Norberg in Rivista di Filologia e di Istruzione Classica 92, 1964, 297; in his Manuel, p. 114, Norberg once more calls attention to the case. In both places Norberg is discussing a passage in a letter from Frodebert, bishop of Tours (7th century), published by G. J. J. Walstra in Les cinq epitres rimees dans l'appendice des Formules de Sens (Diss., Leiden 1962), p. 66 ff. The letter in question is written to Frodebert's colleague in Paris, bishop Importunus, and expresses Frodebert's complaints about the bad quality of the cereals which Im- portunus had sent to a convent at Tours. The passage of interest here runs quod r ecepisti tam dura, estimasti nos iam vicina morte de fame perire, quando talem annonam voluisti largire. Walstra holds that recipere is here an expression typical of the administration language and translates it by `collect' (`percevoir', pp. 38 and 89 ff.). In Norberg's opinion, however, the case exemplifies the meaning reficere, and Norberg translates the quoted text: "A propos du ble si dur dont tu nous as nourris, tu as bien souhaite nous faire bient& mourir de faim, quand tu as eu la bonte de nous donner ce ble". Norberg refers to the passage in Du Cange's dic- tionary, cited above, and both cases are explained as due to a confusion between recipere and reficere, conditioned by the phonetic resemblance between the words. Thus Norberg, contrary to the assumption made above, does not seem to think that the meaning `feed' in the Du Cange case can be semantically derived from `re- ceive'. To support his theory of a confusion between the two words, Norberg adduces examples of the type saltim, used in the same sense as saltuatim. Most of the examples are, however, not convincing parallels, since they—unlike re- ciperelreficere—are derived from basic morphemes which not only were no doubt considered correct, but also generally are correct, such as ianuarius for ianitor, irritare for irritum facere, iterare for iter facere (itinerari) etc.22 As compared to 21 As regards the instrumental function of de and the ablative, see Hofmann-Szantyr, pp. 126 and 264. An illustrative example in Magister Mathias, Copia exemplorum, Cod. Ups. C 54 fol. Bor Alium dormitantem ad psalmodiam dyabolus de nodo stramineo in faciem percussit. 22 For bibliographical information about this very interesting but far from sufficiently studied feature in the post-classical vocabulary, see E. Löfstedt, Late Latin 157 footnote i . The immense production of new words, so typical of Late and particularly Medieval Latin, naturally led to a number of homonyms. In many of these cases it appears reasonable to assume formal influence from the already existing word—striking cases are, for instance, rogus = rogatus (see A. Pratesi in ALMA 22, 1952, 33 if.) and vectigal = vehiculum (see E. Skard, Målet i Historia Norwegiae, p. 24)— but often it does not seem necessary to suppose such an influence, as for instance in the case of the comparatively common irritare = irritum facere (cf. Thes. 7: 2, 431, 23 ff.; examples from the Revelations in II 8 B and 9 B. In A&P 631 tot sceleribus sum irritatus, however, irritatus is an error for irretitus, as is indicated by the parallel passage on p. 543 michi in tantis et tam grauibus sceleribus 
 
 
 
 
 87 these cases, the verb penetrare used as perpetrare23 seems to be more relevant for the assumed confusion between recipere and reficere, and maybe Norberg's expla- nation gives the right solution to our case as weil. Another conceivable solution of the problematic recipitur is suggested by Blaise's dictionary, in which (s.v. 8) the meanings 'accepter', `admettre', 'supporter' and `pardonner' are listed24 (cf. Habel-Gröbel `vertragen'). At least the meaning `supporter' is theoretically possible, to the extent that it admits the connotation `sustain', or even `take charge of' ("my grace and words, by which the soul is sweetly sustained"). Though there are good arguments in favour of reficitur, which may have been the original reading in our case rev. 12: 8, I adopt the archetypal reading recipitur in the edition, since different arguments can be advanced to support the theory that the usual sense of the verb recipere (`receive') is not exemplified in the passage. The sentence then contains the same verb used with different meanings (reci- piendum ... recipitur), and this may of course appear remarkable; however, that phenomenon has a parallel in int. 7: 19, where the word racionabiliter occurs twice, though in different senses;25 cf. the glossary. rev. 12: i o Sed quia sunt (sc. verba ista) de spiritu meo, quem habuerunt prophete sancti, ideo non est tibi timendum sed gaudendum, nisi forte plus pertimescas de vano nomine mundi quam de pr otr accione verborum meorum diuinorum. The nisi clause of this passage is by Lunden 2, 305 translated by "såframt du icke till äventyrs mera rädes för världens fåfänga namn än för mina gudomliga irretito). With the exception of irritare=irritum facere, the other cases mentioned in Norberg's Manuel (p. 114) lack parallels in the Revelations; on the contrary, the classical meaning is to be instanced for iterare in Ex. 65: 20 (other examples in Petrus de Dacia, p. 19, 27, Bulla canonizacionis, DSS VII 255; Blatt's opinion in ALMA 28, 1958, 214, that "au Moyen Age iterare prend en general le sens de voyager" may be misleading), for mentio in Rev. VII 31: lo, for properare in Rev. I 37: 19, for rogus in Rev. I 51: 19. The word saltem occurs some times in the Bulla canonizacionis, with its classical meaning; besides, a semantic distinction seems to have existed between saltem and saltim, cf. Chronicon Salernitanum (ed. Westerbergh), p. 163, 11 f.  88 ords försmädelse". The word protraccione is thus rendered by 'försmädelse', which is the same word as is used to translate int. 13: 28 contemptu (Lunden 2, 289). However, in no dictionary there is such a meaning of protraccio listed. In earlier Latin the word occurs in the sense of 'extension', 'p rotra ct i o n',26 and in Medieval Latin dictionaries the word is instanced in the meaning of `postponement', 'delay'.27 The word appears in Rev. I 25: 5, Ideo propter maximam caritatem supporto eos usque ad ultimum punctum, ut pena ex longa temporis protraccione tardius eis inchoetur. Here the words temporis protraccione are correctly translated by Lunden 1, 113 by "tidsutdräkt". The verb protrahere, too, can be exemplified in the Reve- lations, and the meaning is throughout `postpone',28 e.g. I 56: 4 protrahis iudicium (Lunden i, 174 "uppskjuter ... domen"), 56: 6 iusticia mea ... protrahitur (Lun- den 1.c. "min rättvisa ... uppskjutes"), II 12 B iudicium ... protrahi videtur (Lun- den 1, 221 "tyckes domen ... utdragas"), III 3o C ad tempus protracta est promissio (Lunden 1, 338 "löftet uppsköts en tid"). With regard to this material the word protraccio in our case would be expected to mean 'prolongation' or `postponement'. How is then the passage to be explained? Did the archetype here contain an error, not corrected in any MS., or, if the archetypal reading is correct, does the word have its expected meaning or is something else intended? An analysis of the context indicates that the text of the archetype is correct and that the word has the mean- ing `postponement'. One of the conciusions drawn above in the introductory chapter was that, in all probability, Birgitta herself arranged the Liber questionum text as it appears in. the Latin redaction, i.e. with the thirteen reuelaciones inserted among the interro- gaciones; in an earlier opinion Birgitta was not responsible for that arrangement (see p. 16 ff.). It will be a separate problem to ascertain whether contextual con- nexions exist between all reuelaciones and the interrogaciones; in the case of rev. 12 there is obviously such a connexion. According to Alphonso (Prol.: 7), the inqui- sitive monk of the interrogaciones existed in reality, and we have thus reason to 26 To the cases listed in Georges' dictionary one may add Cod. Just.  89 believe that Birgitta's vision of the monk on the ladder was initiated by her know- ledge of a real, existing monk and not just a product of her imagination. The Spirit also says to Birgitta at the end of int. 16, the last of the interrogaciones, that the monk adhuc viuit corpore sed non ad diem vnum mansurus est viuus (§ 5o), i.e. it is predicted that the man will not live more than one day.29 This prediction is, from a psycho- logical point of view, nothing but an expression of Birgitta's discomfort vis-a-vis the monk's heresy and a wish to have him punished for it. It would certainly have been very strange, if this had caused the man's death, and it is, therefore, a rea- sonable assumption that Birgitta was later informed that the monk was still alive." In that case, Birgitta must have begun to feel doubtful about her revelations and their character of divine messages, since the prediction from int. 16: 5o in accor- dance with this theory—did not come true. Now, Westman lists some revelations (pp. 136 f. and 145 with footnotes), which were given to Birgitta when she on different grounds took the Lord's words not to have been fulfilled, and apparently rev. 12 is also to be ranged in this category of revelations. In other words, the man of whom Jesus Christ is speaking in rev. 12 is identical with the inquisitive monk; its psychological background is Birgitta's anxiety as to the accomplishment of the prediction made by the Spirit in int. 16: so, and an intelligible wish to have that prediction elucidated. Already in § i Birgitta is reproved for lacking reliance, Cur turbaris, quod illum tam pacienter supporto? Nescis, quia graue est eternaliter ardere? The last sentence rather clearly indicates Jesus' decision to punish the man, even though the punishment is being postponed. In § 9 Birgitta is exhorted not to have any doubts about the words she has heard; she must stand firm in her faith and understand that these words are not de spiritu mundi huius, which Birgitta no doubt had feared. This interpretation gives the explanation of the expression de protrac- cione verborum meorum: the fulfilment of the prediction from int. 16: so is post- poned, but in due time it will be realized.31 We may then translate the nisi clause in rev. 12: 10, "if you perchance are not more anxious about the vain name of the world than of the postponement of my words": Birgitta has to consider Jesus' words and prophecies more than wordly vanity, even if she does not know anything about the time of their fulfilment. In this interpretation rev. 12 can be said to imply a sort of correction of what had been revealed to Birgitta in int. 16, and one may suitably refer to a parallel in Rev. VII 7, where Virgin Mary appears to Birgitta, giving her a message which she has to forward to a certain Franciscan. In § 16 Birgitta is informed that multi summi pontifices fuerunt ante lohannem papam, qui sunt in inferno. It is evident that these words were by the friar taken to mean that the soul of the pope John also was in Hell, but that idea is corrected in the following revelation, Rev. VII 8: i "Dic illi fratri amico meo, quod non est tibi licitum scire, 29 As regards ad vnum diem, cf. my article Zeitdifferenzbestimmungen mit per in birgittinischen Texten (Eranos 64, 1966), p. mo f. 39 This implies that not all of the reuelaciones can have been revealed to Birgitta in immediate connexion with the interrogaciones; cf. above, p. 18. 31 Cf. the heading, ipse (sc. Christus) sentenciam iusticie differt ... 
 
 
 
 
 90 vtrum anima pape Iohannis XXII. sit in inferno aut in celo": the friar had obviously asked Birgitta whether his interpretation of Rev. VII 7: 16 was really justified. A parallel to rev. 12: i o is furnished by Rev. 132:5 " Ergo" , inquit (sc. Dominus), "probas in te ipsa omnia esse vera, que tibi dixeram. Quid ergo times vel cur sollici- taris, quia pr o t r aho ea, que facienda tibi dixi? Considera pr ophet as, considera apostolos et sanctos doctores! Numquid inuenerunt in me aliquid nisi veritatem? Ideo non curauerunt de mundo...". The meaning is: since you know that all my words to you are true, you must not be anxious if I postpone certain matters; take the prophets etc. as a pattern, they relied upon my words and did not care for the world. The verb protraho is to be compared with protraccione in our case, in both places the prophets are referred to, and as the prophets did not care for the world, Birgitta must not be anxious de vano nomine mundi. In the case of Rev. I 32: 5, too, Lunden gives an incorrect translation, in rendering protraho by "jag framdrager" ( i , 126).32 This analysis not only indicates that the archetype presents a correct reading in rev. 12: z 0, but it also indicates that the opinion, advanced and justified above on p. 17 ff., viz. that the Latin redaction of the Liber questionum reflects Birgitta's own arrangement, is possible to combine with an examination of the inserted reuela- ciones: at least rev. 12 is most easily explained with the background that is given by int. 16. The strong contextual connexion which has here been assumed for those two texts, makes it impossible to accept the idea held by Ekwall 85, that rev. 12 and rev. 13 constitute some sort of redactional or transitional chapters. rev. i3:R ... de virtute illorum quinque locorum sacrorum, que (v qui pn) sunt in Iherusalem et Bethleem The reading of the archetype was obviously locorum ... qui here, but in all probability qui was an unintentional error for que. There are many cases of the plural form loca, so we have no reason to believe that this noun did not take its normal neuter gender in this place. Later in the heading the five places mentioned are referred to by illa loca, and in the text the neuter gender of these loca is evident in § 3 illa and § 23 ista loca. Further examples of this normal usage are given by Rev, ea and alla loca sancta, que respectively). A theoretical possi- VII 4: 6, 6: 2 (loca bility of defending the archetypal qui would be to assume an influence from the masculine gender in the singular (cf. rev. 13: 19-22), but the idea of an uninten- 32 Errors in Lunden's translation have been listed above on pp. 18, 26, 81 n. i i, 84 f. (two cases). and 87 n. 25. To those cases the following mistranslations may be added, int. IO: 2: Lunden 2, 275 adds the words "ändå" and "dock", illogical in the context; rev. 6: 9 Quibus sic inuolutus est: not translated (2, 282); int. 13: 39 nec sibi sed aliis didicerunt, "de lärde sålunda icke sig själva utan andra" (z, 29o). The meaning is "they did not learn for themselves but for others", i.e. their knowledge made them important in other people's eyes, but it was not used by them in the interest of their own personal improvement (Klockars 132 has the same misinterpretation); int. 14: 28 aut expectandi: not translated (2, 294); int. 14: 32 mundanda translated as if it were mundana (2, 294); int. 15: 14 diuerticula (cf. the glossary), "mångahanda förehavanden" (2, 296).

 I10 7 0 75 LIBRI QUINTI INT. 6-7 perfectam habet nocendi proximo suo, hic similis est dyabolo eiusque membrum est et instrumentum. z6 Cui, scilicet dyabolo, facerem iniu- riam, si eius seruum sine iusticia ab eo auferrem. 27 Ergo, sicut ego instrumento meo ytor ad quecumque michi placita, sic iusticia est, vt dyabolus in eo, qui vult esse membrum eius magis quam meum, operetur et faciat, quod suum est, aut ad purgacionem aliorum aut ad perficiendam maliciam suam, me sic permittente et peccato exigente.» INTERROGACIO SEPTIMA Questio prima.  116 5 LIBRI QUINTI REV. 3 Reuelacio tercia, in qua Christus loquens beate Birgitte sponse sue dat quandam doctrinam similitudinariam de medico vero curatore et de falso medico interfectore et de homine extimatore dicens, quod homo, qui recipit secum peccatores, si dat eis auxilium aut materiam peccandi et moriantur in peccato, Deus exiget mortem animarum eorum de manu illius. Si vero recipit eos, vt cessent a peccato et instruantur ab eo in virtutibus, et isti emendantur per eius doctrinam, habebunt ille et ipsi magnum meritum a Deo. Filius Dei loquitur: »Vbi infirmus est in domo, si ad eum magistralis medicus ingreditur, cicius ex signis exterioribus perpendit, qualem io habet infirmitatem. 2 Medicus igitur sciens infirmitatem infirmi, si dat ei medicamentum, quo mors prouenit, arguitur tamquam interfector et non est verus medicus. 3 Si vero aliquis sciens mederi exercet me- dicinam propter remuneracionem mundi, mercedem non habebit a me. Si vero qui propter honorem et amorem meum medicinam exercet, 15 teneor ego ei mercedem reddere. 4 Si vero aliquis non est magister in medicina sed secundum extimacionem suam credit illa et illa valere infirmo et dat ei pia intencione, hic non est arguendus vt interfector, si moritur infirmus, sed vt fatuus et presumptuosus. 5 Si vero conualescit infirmus ex medicina fatui, tunc ille non tenetur habere mercedem 20 magistri sed extimatoris, quia non dedit medicinam secundum scien- ciam sed secundum extimacionem. 6 Ecce, quid ista significant, dicam tibi. Homines illi noti tibi sunt spiritualiter infirmi et inclinati ad superbiam et cupiditatem sequentes propriam voluntatem. 7 Si igitur amicus eorum, quem ego comparo medico, tribuit eis auxilium et consilium, quo in superbia et ambicione 25 Rev. 3: 13 n Gh (exc. r F Gh linn. 1-7; cfr pp. 68, 71 sq. et infra). sponse sue beate brigide y K q i in libro questionum post tercia add. v 3 spiritualem post eorum add. 5 exigit 0 v extimacione y medico om. 0 illi et ipsi Ab y illi ipsi P 7 mendantur P 6 et (ante isti) om.  LIBRI QUINTI INT. 9 119 pre omni creatura dilexi eam. Hoc ideo est, quia in ipsa speciale insigne 20 virtutum inuentum est. 9 Sicut enim, vbi ignis accenditur lignis plurimis circumpositis, illud cicius inflammatur et comburitur, quod habilius et efficacius est ad comburendum, sic et in Maria fuit. _ro Quando enim ignis amoris diuini, qui in se incommutabilis et eternus est, accendi et apparere cepit et deitas incarnari voluit, nulla creatura ad hunc ignem 25 amoris percipiendum habilior et efficacior erat quam virgo Maria, quia nulla creatura tanta caritate arsit sicut ipsa. ii Et quamuis caritas eius in fine temporum reuelata et ostensa sit, tamen ante principium mundi preuisa est. 12 Et sic in deitate ab eterno prefinitum est, quod, sicut nullus ei in caritate inuentus est similis, sic et nullus ei in gracia 30 et benediccione esset equalis.» 13 Responsio questionis secunde. »Item, cur angelo dedi spiritum sine carne, respondeo: In principio et ante tempora et secula creaui spiritus, vt in libero arbitrio stantes secundum voluntatem meam gauderent de bonitate et gloria mea. 14 Quorum quidam superbientes de bono 35 fecerunt sibi malum, voluntatem liberam mouentes inordinate. Et quia nichil malum erat in natura et creacione nisi inordinacio voluntatis proprie, ideo ceciderunt. /5 Alii vero spirituum elegerunt sub me Deo suo in humilitate stare; ideo et perpetuam stabilitatem meruerunt. 16 Quia dignum et iustum est, vt ego Deus, qui spiritus increatus sum et 40 omnium creator et Dominus, habeam eciam spiritus subtiliores et agi- liores aliis creaturis michi obsequentes. 17 Verum quia non decuit me habere diminucionem in exercitu meo, ideo creaui aliam creaturam, scilicet hominem, loco eorum, qui ceciderunt, que libero arbitrio et bona voluntate promereretur eandem dignitatem, quam angeli deserue- 45 runt. 18 Itaque, si homo haberet animam et non carnem, non posset 21 vbi om. y 20 est om.  LIBRI QUINTI REV. 5 I29 Reuelacio quinta in libro questionum, in qua Christus loquens sponse sue beate Birgitte instruit eam, quod non sit sollicita circa curam diuiciarum terrenarum, et informat eam de paciencia habenda tempore tribulacionis cum virtute perfecte annichilacionis et humilitatis. Filius Dei loquitur sponse dicens: »Attende tibi diligenter!» At illa respondit: »Quare?» Cui Dominus ait: »Quia mundus mittit ad te quatuor seruos te volentes decipere. 2 Primus est sollicitudo diuiciarum. Huic, cum venerit, responde: 'Diuicie transitorie sunt, de quibus tanto major reddenda est racio, quo plus habundant. Ideo non curo de eis, quia non sequuntur possessorem sed relinquunt.' 3 Secundus seruus est amissio diuiciarum et dampnum rerum concessarum. Huic responde sic: 'Qui diuicias dedit, ipse et abstulit; ipse nouit, quid michi expedit. Fiat voluntas eius!' 4 Tercius seruus est tribulacio mundi. Huic sic dicito: `Benedictus sis tu Deus meus, qui me tribulari permittis. 5 Per tribu- laciones enim cognosco, quod tua sum, quia ideo tribulari permittis in presenti, vt parcas in futuro. Propterea tribue michi pacienciam et forti- tudinem sustinendi.' 6 Quartus seruus est despectus et obprobria. Hiis responde taliter: 'Deus solus bonus est et ipsi debetur omnis honor. Ego autem, que feci omnia opera vilia et mala, vnde aut cur michi honor, que magis omni obprobrio digna sum, quia tota vita mea blas- phemauit Deum? 8 Aut quid plus valet michi honor quam obprobrium, nisi quod excitat superbiam et minuit humilitatem et obliuiscitur Deus?  1 34 s LIBRI QUINTI REV. 6 Reuelacio sexta in libro questionum, in qua Christus loquens sponse sue beate Birgitte instruit eam dicens, quod in vita spirituali labore et vigorosa perseuerancia et acquiescere cum humilitate consilio senioris, resistendo viriliter temptacionibus, acquiritur requies mentis et eterna gloria. Et ponit exemplum de Jacob, qui seruiuit pro Rachel. Nam dicit, quod quibusdam veniunt fortissime temptaciones in principio conuersionis ad vitam spiri- tualem, quibusdam veniunt in medio tempore vite spiritualis et circa finem. Et ideo timendum et cum humilitate in virtutibus et labore vsque ad finem perseuerandum est. Filius loquitur: »Scriptum est, quod Iacob seruiuit pro Rachel et videbantur sibi dies pauci pre amoris magnitudine, quia magnitudo amoris labores alleuiabat. z Verum cum Iacob credebat se assequi desi- derabile suum, circumuentus est. Nec tamen adhuc a labore destitit, quia amor de difficultate non causatur, donec assequitur, quod optat. 1 5 3 Sic est et in spiritualibus. Multi enim, vt optineant celestia, laborant viriliter oracionibus et piis laboribus, sed cum ad contemplacionis quietem pertingere credunt, inuoluuntur temptacionibus; accrescunt tribulaciones, et vbi se quasi perfectos arbitrabantur, inueniunt se ex toto imperfectos. 4 Nec mirum.  LIBRI QUINTI INT. 12 B 139 et obediencia bone voluntatis. 27 Transmutata ergo voluntate inchoate 8o sunt due vie. Vna ducebat ad celum, alia abducebat; obediencia duxit ad celum, inobediencia seduxit. z8 Quia ergo in bominis arbitrio erat eleccio boni et mali, scilicet obedire et non obedire, ideo peccauit, quia aliter voluit quam ego Deus volui eum velle. 29 Vt ergo homo saluare- tur, iustum et dignum fuit, vt aliquis talis veniret, qui et redimeret, qui 85 et obedienciam perfectam haberet et innocentum et in quo, qui vellent, possent ostendere caritatem et, qui vellent, maliciam. 30 Sed ad redi- mendum homines non debuit mitti angelus, quia ego Deus gloriam meam alteri non tribuo. Nec inuentus est homo, qui pro se ipso posset placare me, et minus pro aliis.  148 LIBRI QUINTI INT. 13 fructificabat. 45 Cui dixit amicus suus: 'Minor', inquit, 'cum sis sapiens et diues, cur agros tuos diligencius non excolis aut cur non tradis aliis excolendos.' 46 Respondit ille: 'Alter agrorum, quantamcumque dili- I20 genciam exhibuero, nichil producit nisi herbas pessimas, quas bestie nociue occupant et deturpant locum; 47 cui si adhibuero pinguedinem, tantum lasciuiendo insolescit, quod, eciam si modicum frumenti pro- duxerit, plures ascendunt zizanie, quas dedignor colligere, quia fru- mentum non desidero nisi purum. 48 Ergo consulcius est agrum talem 125 dimittere incultum, quia tunc bestie non occupant locum nec bestie occultant se in herbis, et si alique herbe amare pullulant, vtile est pro ouibus, quia gustatis illis discunt suauia non fastidire. 49 Alter vero ager secundum temperiem temporum dispositus est. Cuius quedam pars est petrosa et indiget pinguedine, alia humida indigens calore, alia 0 13 sicca indigens humore. Ideo secundum qualitatem agri opus meum volo temperare.' 5o Ego itaque Deus similis sum homini isti. Primus autem ager est libera mocio voluntatis data homini, quam magis mouet contra me quam pro me. si Qui et si aliqua placita michi fecerit, in pluribus tamen prouocat me, quia voluntas hominis et mea non concordant. 52 135 Sic et Pharao fecit, qui, cum ex certis signis cognosceret potenciam meam, nichilominus firmauit mentem suam contra me standi in malicia sua. 53 Ideo expertus est iusticiam meam, quia qui non bene vtitur minimis, iustum est, vt maximis non glorietur. 54 Alter vero ager est obediencia bone mentis et abieccio voluntatis proprie.  LIBRI QUINTI INT. 13 1 49 est arida in deuocione, expectare debet pluuiam mee gracie diuine. 55 140 Si est petrosa per impacienciam et obduracionem, equanimiter sustineat purgacionem et correpcionem. Si est humida per carnis lasciuiam, amplectatur abstinenciam et sit sicut animal paratum ad voluntatem pos- c sessoris, quia de tali mente ego Deus multum glorior. 56 Ergo, quod aliqui indurantur, hoc facit voluntas hominis michi contraria, quia licet 1 45 ego omnes volo esse saluos, tamen non perficitur, nisi homo personali- ter cooperatus fuerit, conformando omnem voluntatem suam voluntati mee. 57 Quod vero non omnibus datur equalis processus et gracia, hoc est occultum iudicium meum, qui scio et modero vnicuique, quid ei expedit et debetur, qui et restringo conatum hominis, ne profundius 150 cadat. 58 Nam multi habent talentum gracie, qui operari sufficerent, sed renuunt. Alii abstinent a peccato timore supplicii et quia facultatem peccandi non habent vel quia peccatum non delectat eos. Ideo aliquibus non tribuuntur dona maiora, quia ego, qui noui solus mentes hominum, 155 scio distribuere dona mea.» 59 Responsio questionis sexte. »Item, cur mali quandoque prosperantur in mundo magis quam boni, respondeo: Hoc est indicium magne pa- ciencie et caritatis mee et probacio iustorum. 6o Nam si solis amicis meis darem temporalia bona, desperarent mali et superbirent boni.  LIBRI QUINTI INT. I3—REV. ISO 9 alter circa finem, respondeo: Ego sum quasi mater, que videns in filiis spem vite aliis dat forciora, aliis leuiora. Hiis vero, de quibus non est spes, eciam compatitur et facit, quantumcumque potest. 63 Sed si filii 170 ex medicamento matris fiunt deteriores, quid necesse est tunc laborare? 64 Sic ego facio homini. Cuius voluntas preuidetur feruencior et humi- litas et stabilitas constancior, huic accedit gracia in principio et subse- quitur in finem. 65 Qui vero inter mala sua eciam conatur et afficit, vt melior fiat, hic meretur vocari circa finem. Qui vero ingratus est, non 175 meretur admitti ad vbera matris.» 5 Reuelacio nona in libro questionum, in qua Christus loquens sponse sue beate Birgitte ostendit ei, qualiter de domo mundi et viciorum est iam erepta et liberata et quod iam est deducta ad habitandum in mansione Spiritus Sancti. Et ideo monet eam, quod conformet se cum eodem Spiritu, perseuerando semper munda, humilis et deuota. Hii parietes maculant, quia opera bona annichilant et abscondunt ab homine faciem Dei. 4 Fumus vero amor est mundi.  LIBRI QUINTI REV. 9—INT. 14 151 numquam tamen saciat nec replet bonitate eterna. 5 Ab hiis igitur tu es abstracta et ducta es in mansionem Spiritus Sancti, qui est in me et ego in eo, qui et concludit te in se. 6 Ipse quippe mundissimus est et formosissimus stabilissimusque, quia omnia sustentat. I O 155 prophetam inobedientem et non comedit ex cadauere sed custodiuit illud. 33 Quod enim leo occidit corpus, quid aliud innuitur nisi per- missio mea diuina, vt inobediencia prophete puniretur? 34 Quod vero 95 leo non comedit de cadauere, ostensio bonorum operum prophete fuit, vt purgatus in presenti in futuro iustus inueniretur. 35 Propterea timeat vnusquisque discutere iudicia mea, quia sicut incomprehensibilis ego sum virtute et potencia, sic terribilis sum in consiliis et iudiciis meis. Me etenim volentes quidam comprehendere in sapiencia sua exciderunt a 100 spe sua.» Reuelacio decima in libro questionum, in qua Christus loquens sponse monet eam, quod non turbetur, si verba sua diuina in reuelacionibus ei data inueniuntur aliquando obscura, aliquando dubia et aliquando incerta, quia hoc fit ex certis causis hic assignatis et ex occulta iusticia diuina. Con- sulit tamen, quod cum paciencia et timore et perseuerancia humilitatis sem- per expectentur euentus et promissiones verborum eius, ne propter ingrati- tudinem reuocetur gracia promissa. Dicit eciam, quod mulla corporaliter dicta sunt, que non corporaliter sed spiritualiter perficientur. A Fillus loquitur ad sponsam: »Noli turbari, si loquor vnum verbum obscurius, aliud expressius aut si aliquem dico nunc seruum meum vel filium et amicum et iterum inuenitur contrarium. z Quia verba mea diuersimode interpretari possunt, sicut dixi tibi de vno, quod manus eius fieret mors eius, et de alio, quod non accederet ad mensam meam amplius. 3 Hec iden dicuntur, quia aut dicturus sum tibi, cur ita dixi, sicut dixi tibi cfr Rev.  LIBRI QUINTI INT. 15 161 probaui eum, quia nullus iustificabitur in conspectu meo nisi per gra- ciam meam.» 4o Responsio questionis sexte. »Item, cur hii, qui spiritum meum ha- bent, peccant, respondeo: Spiritus deitatis mee non est alligatus, sed vbi vult, spirat et, quando vult, recedit nec habitat in vase subdito peccatis sed in eo, qui caritatem habet. 4z Quia ego Deus caritas sum, et vbi ego sum, libertas est. Ergo, qui accipit spiritum meum, peccare potest, si vult, quia omnis homo habet liberum arbitrium. 42 Itaque, quando homo mouet voluntatem suam contra me, spiritus meus, qui est in eo, recedit ab eo aut ipse homo corripitur, vt corrigat voluntatem suam. 43 Sic Balaam voluit maledicere populo meo sed non permisi eum ego. Quamuis enim propheta malus et cupidus erat, tamen loque- batur quandoque bona, non a se sed a spiritu meo. 44 Nam multociens bonis et malis datur donum spiritus mei. Alioquin illi magni eloquentes de tam sublimibus non disputassent, nisi habuissent spiritum meum, nec ita fatue contra me delirassent, nisi contra me sensissent et se ad superbiam inclinassent, volentes scire plura quam debuissent.» 45 Responsio questionis septime. »Item, cur dyabolus magis est presens et adheret aliquibus, respondeo: Dyabolus est quasi lictor et probator iustorum.  164 LIBRI QUINTI INT. 16 INTERROGACIO SEXTADECIMA Questio prima. Item apparuit religiosus qui supra stans in gradu suo et dicens: »0 iudex, quero a te: Cur secundum dictum euangelii edi ponentur ad sinistram, oues ad dexteram tuam? Numquid talibus de- s lectaris?» 2 Questio secunda. »Item, cum tu sis Dej filius coequalis Patri, cur scribitur, quod nec tu nec angeli sciunt horam iudicii?» 3 Questio tercia. »Item, cum Spiritus Sanctus tuus locutus sit in euangelistis, cur tanta est euangeliorum dissonancia?» I° 4 Questio quarta. »Item, cum tanta salus sit toti humano generi in incarnacione tua, cur tanto tempore distulisti incarnari?» Questio quinta. »Item, cum anima hominis melior sit toto mundo, cur vbique et semper non mittis amicos et predicatores tuos?» 6 Responsio questionis prime. Respondit iudex: »Amice, non queris, vt is scias, sed vt sciatur malicia tua. Denique in deitate nichil est carnale nec carnaliter effigiatum, quia deitas mea spiritus est, nec mecum simul boni et mall cohabitare possunt, non magis quam lux simul et tenebre. 7 Sed nec dextera et sinistra in deitate mea est tamquam corporaliter effigiata, sed nec feliciores sunt, qui ad dexteram meam erunt quam ad 20 sinistram, sed per similitudinem hec dicta sunt. 8 Quia per dexteram intelligitur sublimitas mee diuine glorie, per sinistram vero defectus et privacio tocius boni. 9 Sed nec oues vel edi in illa admirabili gloria mea sunt, vbi nichil corporale et inquinatum vel transmutabile est, sed in similitudinibus et figuris animalium multociens scribuntur mores ho- 25 minum, sicut in oue innocencia, in edo lasciuia, idest homo incontinens, 3 dictum euangelii Matth. 25,33 7 scribitur Matth. 24,36; Marc. 13,32 Int.  170 LIBRI QUINTI REV. 12 Reuelacio duodecima in libro questionum, in qua Christus loquens sponse sue beate Birgitte dicit ei, quod non debet turbari ex eo, quod ipse non facit statim iusticiam super hominem magnum peccatorem, quia ipse sentenciam iusticie differt, vt sua iusticia in illo fienda aliis manifestetur. Dicit eciam, 5 quod verba sua diuina in isto libro celestium reuelacionum contenta prius debent crescere et vsque ad plenam maturitatem fructificare et postea producere effectum suum et virtutem in mundo. Que quidem verba sunt sicut oleum in lampade, idest in anima virtuosa, quibus ipsa impinguatur et super- ueniente Spiritu Sancto eam ardere et splendore mirabili lucere faciunt. lo Subiungit eciam, quod dicta verba reuelacionum prius ascendent et fructi- ficabunt alibi quam in regno Suecie, vbi eidem sponse reuelari diuinitus inceperunt.  Glossarium This glossary lists such words as are completely lacking in Georges' Hand- wörterbuch, but it also contains words which appear in Georges but there signify something else than is applicable in the text. Furthermore, some words have been included as a consequence of a spelling not found in Georges' dictionary. Trivial differences, however, between the classical and the medieval spelling (i.e. e for ae, oe; cf. above, p. 72) have not been taken into consideration. To support the translation (given in Classical Latin, English and Swedish), references are made in most cases to dictionaries or other relevant literature; Rev. VII and Ex. refer to the glossaries included in the modern editions of these revelation books. References to the glossary in Undhagen (see above, p. i i) are indicated by Undh. abextra adv. = extra, 'on the outside', `exter- nally'; 'på utsidan', 'utvärtes' rev. i (bis), rev. 4: 12. (Rev. VII, Ex., Be, SG1 i a, Sr.) abhominabiliter adv. fere = foede, `abomi- nably'; 'avskyvärt' rev. 8:R. (Lm, MW, SG1.) abintra adv. = intra, 'on the inside', 'inter- nally'; 'på insidan', 'invärtes' rev. i: 1.2. (Dief., H—G; cfr SG1.) abortiuum, i n. = fetus qui in utero matris interiit, `stillborn foetus'; 'dödfött foster' rev. 8: 16. (Be 2, MW 2, Nn, SG1, Sr.) abortiuus, i m. = abortiuum (vide supra) rev. 8:R. Rev. VI 28 A. (Ai, Be 2, Nn, SG1.) afficere v. = affectare, `strive after'; 'sträva efter' int. 13: 65.
